                                           TRAFFIC IMPACT ANALYSIS
                                            THE LINK PROJECT
                                            City of Glendale, California
                                                    June 3, 2013


1.0        INTRODUCTION
This traffic analysis has been conducted to identify and evaluate the potential traffic impacts of
The Link project to be located in the City of Glendale, California. The project site comprises
five parcels and is located at the northwest corner of the San Fernando Road/Central Avenue
intersection. The project site location and general vicinity are shown in Figure 1­1.

The traffic analysis follows City of Glendale traffic study guidelines and is consistent with traffic
impact assessment guidelines set forth in the 2010 Congestion Management Program 1. This
traffic analysis evaluates potential project-related traffic impacts at five key intersections in the
vicinity of the project site. The study intersections were determined in consultation with City of
Glendale Department of Public Works Traffic & Transportation Division staff. The Intersection
Capacity Utilization method was used to determine volume-to-capacity ratios and corresponding
Levels of Service at the study intersections. In addition, a review was conducted of Los Angeles
County Metropolitan Transportation Authority intersection and freeway monitoring stations to
determine if a Congestion Management Program transportation impact assessment analysis is
required for the proposed project.

This study (i) presents existing traffic volumes, (ii) forecasts existing-plus-project traffic
volumes, (iii) forecasts future traffic volumes with and without the proposed project, (iv)
determines project-related impacts, and (v) recommends mitigation measures, if necessary.

1.1        Study Area
Based on direction from City of Glendale staff, a total of five study intersections have been
identified for evaluation. These study locations provide local access to the study area and define
the extent of the boundaries for this traffic impact investigation. Further discussion of the
existing street system and study area is provided in Section 4.0 herein.

The general location of the project in relation to the study locations and surrounding street
system is presented in Figure 1­1. The traffic analysis study area is generally comprised of
those locations which have the greatest potential to experience significant traffic impacts due to
the proposed project as defined by the Lead Agency. In the traffic engineering practice, the
study area generally includes those intersections that are:

           a.         Immediately adjacent or in close proximity to the project site;



1
 2010 Congestion Management Program, Los Angeles County Metropolitan Transportation Authority, October
2010.

           b.         In the vicinity of the project site that are documented to have current or projected
                      future adverse operational issues; and

           c.         In the vicinity of the project site that are forecast to experience a relatively greater
                      percentage of project-related vehicular turning movements.

The locations selected for analysis were based on the above criteria, proposed project peak hour
vehicle trip generation, the anticipated distribution of project vehicular trips, and existing
intersection/corridor operations.

2.0        PROJECT DESCRIPTION
2.1        Site Location
The project site is located at 3901-3915 San Fernando Road, within the San Fernando Corridor
Redevelopment Project Area of the City of Glendale. The proposed site is generally bounded by
a CVS Pharmacy to the north, Central Avenue to the south, San Fernando Road to the east, and
the existing alleyway and commercial uses to the west.

2.2        Existing Project Site
The existing project site is currently occupied by a two-story, 16,000 square-foot commercial
building, a 14,380 square-foot industrial building and associated parking areas. The existing
buildings will be removed to accommodate development of the proposed project. It should be
noted that approximately 1,000 square feet of the 14,380 square-foot industrial building is
currently vacant.

Vehicular access to the existing parcels is currently provided via a total of five driveways: two
driveways on San Fernando Road and three driveways on the existing alleyway that borders the
project site to the west. The existing driveways on San Fernando Road are located along the
easterly property frontage and provide access to the existing commercial building and associated
parking area. The existing driveways on the existing alleyway are located along the westerly
property frontage and provide access to the existing industrial and commercial buildings and
associated parking areas.

2.3         Proposed Project Description
The proposed project consists of the construction of a mixed-use development with 142
apartment dwelling units and approximately 16,600 square feet of ground floor commercial use.
The residential component will include a total of 23 junior one-bedroom units, 84 one-bedroom
units and 35 two-bedroom units within four levels. Ancillary uses for the residential use will
include a courtyard and pool area.

Four options are currently proposed for the ground floor commercial component of the project as
described below:

      ·    Option No. 1: Studio without Mezzanine Parking

                o 5,000 SF Studio Space

                o 11,600 SF Retail

      ·    Option No. 2: Studio with Mezzanine Parking

                o 5,000 SF Studio Space

                o 11,100 SF Retail

LINSCOTT, LAW & GREENSPAN, engineers                                                 LLG Ref. 1-12-3981-1
                                                                                         The Link Project
                                                                             O:\JOB_FILE\3981\Report\3981rpt.doc


                                               -4-
     ·     Option No. 3: Live/Work without Mezzanine Parking

                o 8,500 SF Live/Work (8 Units)

                o 8,600 SF Retail

     ·     Option No. 4: Live/Work with Mezzanine Parking

                o 8,500 SF Live/Work (8 Units)

                o 8,100 SF Retail

Since the Applicant is not certain at this time which option is the most likely to be constructed on
the site, this traffic analysis considers the "worst-case" scenario in terms of potential vehicular
trip generation. Thus, the assessment of traffic impacts on the local street system can be
considered conservative and affords the Applicant the most flexibility in terms of potential
tenancy without having to revise the corresponding environmental documentation. See Section
7.1, Project Traffic Generation, for additional discussion.

Parking for the project is planned to be provided within a parking garage with both subterranean
and at-grade parking levels. Access to the residential parking will be provided via a single full
access driveway off of the existing alleyway that borders the project site to the west. Access to
the commercial project component will be via a full access driveway on San Fernando Road and
a full access driveway off of the existing alleyway located along the westerly property frontage.
Further discussion of the proposed project site access and circulation scheme is provided in
Section 3.0. Project completion and occupancy is projected to be completed by year 2016. The
ground floor site plans for each option are shown in Figures 2-1 through 2-4, respectively.

3.0        SITE ACCESS AND CIRCULATION
The proposed site access scheme for the project is displayed in Figure 2­1. Descriptions of the
existing and proposed site access and circulation schemes are provided in the following
subsections.

3.1        Existing Site Access
Vehicular access to the existing parcels is currently provided via a total of five driveways: two
driveways on San Fernando Road and three driveways on the existing alleyway that borders the
project site to the west. Brief descriptions of the existing site driveways are provided below:

      ·    Existing San Fernando Road Driveways:

           -    San Fernando Road Northerly Driveway: The existing site driveway on San
                Fernando Road is located along the easterly property frontage and provides access to
                the existing 16,000 square-foot commercial building and associated parking area.
                The San Fernando Road northerly driveway accommodates full access (i.e., right-turn
                and left-turn ingress and egress turning movements).

           -    San Fernando Road Southerly Driveway: The existing site driveway on San Fernando
                Road is located approximately mid-way along the easterly property frontage and also
                provides access to the parking area for the 16,000 square-foot commercial building.
                The San Fernando Road southerly driveway accommodates full access (i.e., right-turn
                and left-turn ingress and egress turning movements).

      ·    Existing Public Alley Driveways

           -    Public Alley Northerly Driveway: The existing public alley northerly driveway is
                located along the east side of the public alley that borders the project site to the west,
                at the northwest corner of the project site. The public alley northerly driveway
                provides access to the loading dock area associated with the 16,000 square-foot
                commercial building. The Public Alley northerly driveway accommodates full access
                (i.e., right-turn and left-turn ingress and egress turning movements).

           -    Public Alley Middle Driveway: The existing public alley middle driveway is located
                along the east side of the public alley that borders the project site to the west,
                approximately midway between the Central Avenue and project site northerly
                boundary. The public alley middle driveway provides access to the surface parking
                area of the 16,000 square-foot commercial building. The Public Alley middle
                driveway accommodates full access (i.e., right-turn and left-turn ingress and egress
                turning movements).

           -    Public Alley Southerly Driveway: The existing public alley southerly driveway is
                located along the east side of the public alley that borders the project site to the west,
                near the southwest corner of the project site. The public alley southerly driveway

3.2        Proposed Project Site Access
Access to the proposed project site will be provided via a total of three main driveways: two
driveways that will be provided off of the existing public alley (i.e., the north-south alley that
extends that borders the project site to the west) and one driveway along San Fernando Road.
Descriptions of the planned project site access points are provided in the following paragraphs.

      ·    Public Alley Residential Driveway:

           This project driveway will be located along the east side of the public alley that borders
           the project site to the west, at the northwest corner of the project site. This project
           driveway will provide access to the residential subterranean parking garage planned as
           part of the proposed project. This driveway will accommodate full access (i.e., right-turn
           and left-turn ingress and egress turning movements). The project site driveway would be
           constructed to City of Glendale design standards.

      ·    Public Alley Commercial Driveway:

           This project driveway will be located along the east side of the public alley that borders
           the project site to the west, near the southwest corner of the project site. This project
           driveway will provide access to the commercial parking area for the proposed project.
           This driveway will accommodate full access (i.e., right-turn and left-turn ingress and
           egress turning movements). The project site driveway would be constructed to City of
           Glendale design standards.

      ·    San Fernando Road Driveway:

           This project driveway will be located along the west side of San Fernando Road, at the
           northeast portion of the project site. This project driveway will provide access to the
           commercial parking area. This driveway will accommodate full access (i.e., right-turn
           and left-turn ingress and egress turning movements). The project site driveway would be
           constructed to City of Glendale design standards.

additional access driveway along the existing public alley will be provided for access to the
potential mezzanine parking level of the proposed project. A description of the potential
mezzanine site access driveway is provided in the following paragraph.

4.0        PROJECT PARKING
This section summarizes the project parking requirements based on application of the Code
requirements and a forecast of the commercial parking demand. As previously mentioned, a
total supply of 244 parking spaces is planned to be provided on-site. The parking analysis
provides an assessment of the adequacy of the proposed parking supply to satisfy the forecast
parking demand for commercial patrons to the site. Please note that Code required parking for
any development project is ultimately determined by the City of Glendale.

4.1        Project Parking Supply
As previously described, four commercial options are proposed for the project. The number of
parking spaces provided on-site differ by commercial development option as outlined below:

      ·    Option No. 1 (Studio without Mezzanine Parking): 244 total parking spaces

      ·    Option No. 2 (Studio with Mezzanine Parking): 260 total parking spaces

      ·    Option No. 3 (Live/Work without Mezzanine Parking): 244 total parking spaces

      ·    Option No. 4 (Live/Work with Mezzanine Parking): 260 total parking spaces

4.2        Code Parking Requirement
The City of Glendale requirements for apartment and commercial land uses are set forth in
Section 30.32.050 of the Glendale Municipal Code (i.e., Code). As indicated in the Municipal
Code, the following Code parking requirements are applicable to the proposed project land use
components:

      ·    Apartment:
              - One-bedroom and two-bedroom units: Two (2.0) spaces for each unit.
              - Guest Parking: One-quarter (0.25) space for each unit.

      ·    General Retail Use:
              - Four (4.0) spaces for each 1,000 square feet of floor area.

      ·    Industrial:
              - Two (2.0) spaces for each 1,000 square feet of floor area.

      ·    Live/Work:
              - Three (3.0) spaces for the first 2,000 square feet of floor area.
              - Three (3.0) spaces for each additional 1,000 square feet of floor area.

In addition, when a housing development meets the minimum requirements to qualify for a
density bonus, the project Applicant may apply for a parking concession based on the following
ratios inclusive of handicapped parking and guest parking:


LINSCOTT, LAW & GREENSPAN, engineers                                                    LLG Ref. 1-12-3981-1
                                                                                            The Link Project
                                                                                O:\JOB_FILE\3981\Report\3981rpt.doc


                                                 - 13 -
      ·    Zero to One (1) Bedroom: One (1.0) space for each unit

      ·    Two (2) to Three (3) Bedrooms: Two (2.0) spaces for each unit

      ·    Four (4) to Five (5) Bedrooms: Two and a half (2.5) spaces for each unit

A summary of the Code parking requirements for the Option 1 Project is outlined in Table 4-1.
Direct application of the Code parking rates to the Option 1 Project yields a total Code parking
requirement of 232 parking spaces (176 residential spaces and 56 commercial spaces). Thus, the
proposed parking supply of 244 spaces for the Option 1 Project (Studio without Mezzanine
Parking) would satisfy the parking requirements pursuant to the Code (i.e., a surplus of 12 spaces
would occur with approval by the City of a density bonus and parking concession).

Similarly, a summary of the Code parking requirements for the Option 3 Project is outlined in
Table 4-2. Direct application of the Code parking rates to the Option 3 Project yields a total
Code parking requirement of 233 parking spaces (176 residential spaces and 57 commercial
spaces). Thus, the proposed parking supply of 244 spaces for the Option 3 Project (Live/Work
without Mezzanine Parking) satisfies the parking requirements pursuant to the Code, with a
surplus of 11 spaces forecast (i.e., with a density bonus and parking concession).

4.3        Commercial Parking Demand
The commercial space is expected to generate a significant degree of walk-in patronage both from
within the project, and from other surrounding uses due to the project's proximity to adjacent retail
and commercial uses. The commercial component of the project will be located on the ground level
of the site and is envisioned to serve the residential tenants and guests, as well as the adjacent
commercial and residential buildings. In addition, the project site is located in an area served by
numerous transit routes and is within approximately 0.25 miles from the existing Larry Zarian
Transportation Center (LZTC), formerly known as the Glendale Amtrak/Metrolink Station. The
LZTC serves as a central transportation hub for the City of Glendale for various public
transportation systems such as Amtrak, Metrolink, Greyhound, Metro, and the Glendale Beeline.
According to the criteria outlined in Appendix F of the 2010 Congestion Management Program for
Commercial Mixed-Use Development around Transit Centers, a vehicle trip reduction factor of
20% is applicable to the proposed project. Thus, based on these factors, the transit reduction for the
commercial component of the project was estimated to be approximately 20 percent (20%) during
the peak periods. Therefore, for purposes of this study, it is estimated that 37 parking spaces would
adequately accommodate the commercial component of the project (i.e., 80% of the highest retail
component parking requirement, which occurs under the Option 1 Project [0.80 x 46 spaces = 37
spaces).

4.4        Residential Parking Demand
Although not required as part of the density bonus application, guest parking spaces for the
residential component of the project will be provided on-site. The parking demand ratio
identified in ULI Shared Parking is 0.15 guest spaces per residential unit. This would be

expected to be more than adequate for the project, particularly given the project's location and
proximity to downtown as well as to transit service and the Larry Zarian Transportation Center
(see Section 5.4 of this report for additional discussion regarding existing transit service in
proximity to the project site). It should be noted that the ULI parking ratio for guests is
consistent with or higher than that of other adjacent jurisdictions. For example, the City of
Pasadena Municipal Code indicates a parking ratio of one guest parking space for each 10 units
for multi-family residential projects both within the Central District, as well as other areas of the
City. In addition, the City of Glendale undertook a review of parking demand for an affordable
housing project which produced a parking demand rate of 0.17 spaces per unit. It is important to
note that this project consisted of two and three bedroom units, was located outside of the
downtown area, and is not comparable to the proposed project for these reasons. Therefore, a
guest parking ratio of 0.15 spaces per residential unit was determined applicable for use in the
parking demand analysis for The Link project. This results in a parking demand of 21 guest
parking spaces for the residential units. These spaces are planned to be located within the B1
level of the subterranean parking garage, outside of the gated resident parking area.

4.5        Summary of Parking Analysis
Application of the commercial parking demand transit reduction as mentioned above yields a
parking requirement of 37 spaces for the commercial component (i.e., retail) under the Option 1
Project. In addition, although not required as part of the density bonus application, a guest
parking demand of 21 parking spaces was determined for the residential component. Combined
with the residential parking requirement of 176 spaces and a studio parking requirement of 10
spaces, a total peak parking demand of 244 spaces is forecast for the Option 1 Project. Thus, the
proposed parking supply of 244 parking spaces is expected to meet the forecast peak parking
demand. As such, no significant parking impacts are forecast due to the development of the
project.

5.0        EXISTING STREET SYSTEM
5.1        Regional Highway System
Regional access in the project vicinity is provided by the Glendale (SR-2) Freeway, Ventura
(SR-134) Freeway and Golden State (I-5) Freeway. Brief descriptions of the subject freeways
are provided in the following paragraphs.

SR-2 (Glendale) Freeway is a north/south oriented freeway that extends from just south of the I-
5 Freeway near Echo Park to just north of the I-210 Freeway near La Canada Flintridge. The
northerly terminus of the freeway occurs at Foothill Boulevard. Northbound and southbound on-
and off-ramps are provided at San Fernando Road, approximately 1.50 miles southeast of the
project site. The SR-2 Freeway generally provides four mixed-flow travel lanes in each direction
in the project site vicinity.

SR-134 (Ventura) Freeway is an east-west oriented freeway that extends from the I-210 Freeway
in Pasadena to the US-101 in North Hollywood. Four mixed-flow travel lanes and one high
occupancy vehicle (HOV) lane are provided in each direction on the SR-134 Freeway in the
Glendale area. Full interchanges are provided at Central Avenue/Brand Boulevard and Glendale
Avenue/Monterey Road. The SR-134 Freeway ramps at Central Avenue and Brand Boulevard
are connected by one-way connector roadways (Goode Avenue and Sanchez Drive). At Central
Avenue, a westbound on-ramp and an eastbound off-ramp are provided in connection with the
Goode Avenue and Sanchez Drive freeway one-way frontage roadways. At Brand Boulevard, a
westbound off-ramp and an eastbound on-ramp are provided in connection with these two
freeway frontage roadways. At Glendale Avenue, an eastbound off-ramp, a southbound to
eastbound loop on-ramp and a northbound to eastbound diamond on-ramp are provided. The
westbound on- and off-ramps are provided at Monterey Road.

I-5 (Golden State) Freeway is a north-south oriented freeway that extends between northern and
southern California. The I-5 Freeway runs alongside the Los Angeles River west of the project
site, interchanging with the SR-134 Freeway to the north and the SR-2 Freeway to the south.
Five mainline travel lanes are generally provided in each direction on the I-5 Freeway in the
Glendale area. Full interchanges are provided at Los Feliz Boulevard and Glendale Boulevard,
less than one mile southwest of the project site.

5.2        Local Street System
Immediate access to the project site is via Central Avenue, San Fernando Road and the north-
south alleyway that borders the project site to the west. The following five study intersections
were selected for analysis by City of Glendale Traffic & Transportation Division staff in order to
determine potential impacts related to the proposed project:

           1. Gardena Avenue/Los Feliz Boulevard
           2. San Fernando Road/Los Feliz Boulevard
           3. Central Avenue/Los Feliz Boulevard

5.3        Roadway Descriptions
A brief description of the important roadways in the project site vicinity is provided in the
following paragraphs.

Gardena Avenue is a north-south oriented roadway that is located west of the project site.
Gardena Avenue is designated as a Local Street within the study area in the Circulation Element
of the City of Glendale General Plan. One through travel lane is provided in each direction on
Gardena Avenue within the study area. Gardena Avenue is posted for a speed limit of 25 miles
per hour (MPH) near the site.

San Fernando Road is a north-south oriented roadway that borders the project site to the east.
San Fernando Road is designated as a Major Arterial from the westerly City boundary to the
southerly City boundary in the Circulation Element of the City of Glendale General Plan. Two
through travel lanes are generally provided in each direction in the project vicinity. Exclusive
left-turn lanes are provided in both directions at major intersections in the project vicinity. San
Fernando Road is posted for a speed limit of 35 miles per hour in the project vicinity.

Central Avenue is a north-south oriented roadway that borders the project site to the south and
then extends northeasterly east of San Fernando Road. Central Avenue is designated as a Major
Arterial within the study area in the Circulation Element of the City of Glendale General Plan.
Along the project frontage, one through travel lane is provided in each direction on Central
Avenue. However, at the intersection with San Fernando Road as well at other major
intersections, exclusive left-turn lanes are provided. East of San Fernando Road, Central Avenue
provides two travel lanes in both directions in the project vicinity. Central Avenue is posted for
a speed limit of 35 miles per hour (MPH) near the site.

Los Feliz Road is an east-west roadway that is located north of the project site. Los Feliz Road is
designated as a Major Arterial in the Circulation Element of the City of Glendale General Plan.
Los Feliz Boulevard, the continuation of Los Feliz Road in the City of Los Angeles, is
designated as a Major Highway Class II from the City's easterly limits to Vermont Avenue in the
City of Los Angeles General Plan Transportation Element. Los Feliz Road is posted for a speed
limit of 35 miles per hour within the study area.

Brand Boulevard is a north-south oriented roadway that is located south and east of the project
site. Brand Boulevard is designated as a Major Arterial between Glenoaks Boulevard and the
southerly City boundary in the Circulation Element of the City of Glendale General Plan. Three
through travel lanes are provided in the each direction on Brand Boulevard in the project
vicinity. Exclusive left-turn lanes are provided in both directions on Brand Boulevard at the

Glendale Boulevard is a north-south oriented roadway that is located south of the project site.

5.4        Existing Public Bus Transit Service
Public bus transit service in the project vicinity is currently provided by the Metropolitan
Transportation Authority (Metro) and the City of Glendale Beeline. A summary of the existing
transit routes, including the transit route, destinations and number of buses during the AM and
PM peak hours is presented in Table 5­1. The existing public transit routes in the project
vicinity are illustrated in Figure 5­2.

5.4.1 Metro Bus Transit Services
Metro provides bus transit service along major roadways within the traffic analysis study area:
Central Avenue, Brand Boulevard, Los Feliz Boulevard and San Fernando Road. Metro operates
five local bus transit routes and one Metro Rapid transit route in the vicinity of the project site.
Most of the Metro bus transit routes provide headways of between one and six buses per hour
during the morning and afternoon peak hours.

5.4.2 City of Glendale Bus Transit Services
The City of Glendale provides bus transit service within the study area with its Beeline bus
service. In the traffic analysis study area, Glendale Beeline service is provided along Central
Avenue, Brand Boulevard, Los Feliz Road and San Fernando Road. Glendale Beeline also
provides express service to the Glendale Transportation Center along Brand Boulevard. Glendale
Beeline operates three local transit routes in the immediate vicinity of the project site. Most of
the Beeline transit routes provide headways of three buses per hour during the morning and
afternoon peak hours.

5.4.3 Rail Transit Services
Metrolink operates two commuter rail transit lines which stop and service the existing Larry
Zarian Transportation Center (LZTC), formerly known as the Glendale Amtrak/Metrolink
Station. The Antelope Valley Line runs north-south from Lancaster to the Los Angeles Union
Station, and the Ventura County Line runs east-west from Montalvo to the Los Angeles Union
Station. In addition, Amtrak operates the Pacific Surfliner transit line which stops and services
the GTC. The Pacific Surfliner Line runs north-south from Santa Barbara to San Diego.

7.0        TRAFFIC FORECASTING METHODOLOGY
In order to estimate the traffic impact characteristics of the proposed project, a multi-step process
has been utilized. The first step is trip generation, which estimates the total arriving and
departing traffic volumes on a peak hour and daily basis. For projects, the traffic generation
potential is typically forecast by applying the appropriate vehicle trip generation equations or
rates to the project development tabulation.

The second step of the forecasting process is trip distribution, which identifies the origins and
destinations of inbound and outbound project traffic volumes. These origins and destinations are
typically based on demographics and existing/anticipated travel patterns in the study area.

The third step is traffic assignment, which involves the allocation of project traffic to study area
streets and intersections. Traffic assignment is typically based on minimization of travel time,
which may or may not involve the shortest route, depending on prevailing operating conditions
and travel speeds. Traffic distribution patterns are indicated by general percentage orientation,
while traffic assignment allocates specific volume forecasts to individual roadway links and
intersection turning movements throughout the study area.

With the forecasting process complete and project traffic assignments developed, the impact of
the proposed project is isolated by comparing operational (i.e., Level of Service (LOS))
conditions at selected key intersections using existing and expected future traffic volumes with
and without forecast project traffic. The need for site-specific and/or cumulative local area
traffic improvements can then be evaluated and the significance of the project's impacts
identified.

7.1        Project Trip Generation Summary
As previously mentioned, since the Applicant is not certain at this time which development
program option is the most likely to be constructed on the site, this traffic analysis considers the
"worst-case" scenario in terms of potential vehicular trip generation. Thus, the assessment of
traffic impacts on the local street system can be considered conservative. The proposed project
consists of the construction of a mixed-use development with 142 apartment dwelling units and
approximately 16,600 square feet of ground floor commercial use. Four ground floor
commercial development options are currently under consideration and two consider parking on
the mezzanine level. Traffic volumes expected to be generated by the proposed project during
the weekday AM and PM peak hours, as well as on a daily basis, were estimated using rates
published in the Institute of Transportation Engineers' (ITE) Trip Generation manual 2. Traffic
volumes expected to be generated by the residential component of the proposed project were
based upon rates per number of residential units. Traffic volumes expected to be generated by
the commercial component of the proposed project were based upon rates per 1,000 square feet.
Trip generation average rates for the following uses were used to forecast the traffic volumes
expected to be generated each option of the proposed project:

2
    Institute of Transportation Engineers Trip Generation manual, 9th Edition, 2012.

     ·     ITE Land Use Code 220: Apartment

     ·     ITE Land Use Code 230: Residential Condominium/Townhouse

     ·     ITE Land Use Code 820: Shopping Center

Traffic volumes expected to be generated by the existing uses to be removed from the site during
the weekday AM and PM peak hours, as well as on a daily basis, were also estimated using rates
published in the ITE Trip Generation manual. Trip generation average rates for the following
uses were used to forecast the traffic volumes expected to be generated by the existing uses
currently on-site:

     ·     ITE Land Use Code 710: General Office Building

     ·     ITE Land Use Code 820: Shopping Center

     ·     ITE Land Use Code 110: Light Industrial

It should be noted that approximately 1,000 square feet of the 14,380 square-foot industrial
building is currently vacant and this portion of the building has not been included as part of the
existing use trip generation credit.

A summary of the trip generation forecasts for each development option is summarized in Table
7-1. The trip generation forecasts for the proposed project were submitted for review and
approval by City of Glendale Traffic & Transportation Division staff. As presented in Table 7-1,
Options 1 and 2 for the proposed project result in the highest trip generation potential during the
AM and PM peak hours without and with the mezzanine parking, respectively. The detailed trip
generation forecasts for Options 1, 2, 3 and 4 of the proposed project are provided in Tables 7-2,
7-3, 7-4 and 7-5, respectively.

As presented in Table 7-1, the Option 1 Project is expected to generate a net increase of 47
vehicle trips (5 fewer inbound trips and 52 outbound trips) during the AM peak hour. During the
PM peak hour, the Option 1 Project is expected to generate a net increase of 78 vehicle trips (58
inbound trips and 20 outbound trips). Over a 24-hour period, the Option 1 project is forecast to
generate a net increase of 932 daily trip ends during a typical weekday (466 inbound trips and
466 outbound trips).

As presented in Table 7-1, the Option 2 Project is also expected to generate a net increase of 47
vehicle trips (5 fewer inbound trips and 52 outbound trips) during the AM peak hour. During the
PM peak hour, the Option 2 Project is expected to generate a net increase of 76 vehicle trips (57
inbound trips and 19 outbound trips). Over a 24-hour period, the Option 2Project is forecast to
generate a net increase of 918 daily trip ends during a typical weekday (459 inbound trips and
459 outbound trips).

7.2        Project Trip Distribution
Project traffic volumes both entering and exiting the site have been distributed and assigned to
the adjacent street system based on the following considerations:

      ·    The site's proximity to major traffic corridors (i.e., San Fernando Road, Los Feliz
           Boulevard, Los Feliz Road, Brand Boulevard and Central Avenue),

      ·    Expected localized traffic flow patterns based on adjacent roadway channelization and
           presence of traffic signals,

      ·    Existing intersection traffic volumes,

      ·    Ingress/egress availability at the project site,

      ·    The location of existing and proposed parking areas, and

      ·    Input from City staff.

As described in Sections 2.0 and 3.0, access to the commercial component will be provided via
one driveway on San Fernando Road and one driveway off of the existing public alley, while
access to the residential component of the proposed project will be provided via one driveway
off the existing public alley. As such, two separate traffic distribution patterns were developed
for the proposed project: one for the commercial component and one for the residential
component. The two trip distribution patterns developed for the proposed project were submitted
for review and approval by City of Glendale Traffic & Transportation Division staff.

The project traffic volume distribution percentages for the commercial component during AM
and PM peak hours at the study intersections are illustrated in Figure 7-1. The project traffic
volume distribution percentages for the residential component during the AM and PM peak
hours at the study intersections are illustrated in Figure 7-2. The forecast AM and PM peak hour
project traffic volumes (i.e., the combined commercial and residential volumes) at the study
intersections for the AM and PM peak hours for the Option 1 Project are displayed in Figures 7-
3 and 7-4, respectively. The traffic volume assignments presented in Figures 7-3 and 7-4 reflect
the traffic distribution characteristics shown in Figures 7-1 and 7-2 and the proposed project
traffic generation forecast presented in Table 7-2.

8.0        FUTURE PRE-PROJECT DEVELOPMENT
The forecast of future pre-project conditions was prepared in accordance with procedures
outlined in Section 15130 of the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) Guidelines.
Specifically, the CEQA Guidelines provides two options for developing the future traffic volume
forecast:

           "(A) A list of past, present, and probable future projects producing related or
           cumulative impacts, including, if necessary, those projects outside the control of
           the [lead] agency, or

           (B) A summary of projections contained in an adopted local, regional or statewide
           plan, or related planning document, that describes or evaluates conditions
           contributing to the cumulative effect. Such plans may include: a general plan,
           regional transportation plan, or plans for the reduction of greenhouse gas
           emissions. A summary of projections may also be contained in an adopted or
           certified prior environmental document for such a plan. Such projections may be
           supplemented with additional information such as a regional modeling program.
           Any such document shall be referenced and made available to the public at a
           location specified by the lead agency."

Accordingly, the traffic analysis provides a highly conservative estimate of future pre-project
traffic volumes as it incorporates both the "A" and "B" options outlined in the CEQA Guidelines
for purposes of developing the forecast.

8.1        Related Projects
A forecast of on-street traffic conditions prior to occupancy of the proposed project was prepared
by incorporating the potential trips associated with other known development projects (related
projects) in the area. With this information, the potential impact of the proposed project can be
evaluated within the context of the cumulative impact of all ongoing development. The list of
related projects was based on information on file at the City of Glendale Community
Development Department, City of Los Angeles Department of Transportation, as well as recently
accepted traffic impact analysis reports prepared for projects in the vicinity of the proposed
project site. The list of related projects in the project site area is presented in Table 8­1. The
location of the related projects is shown in Figure 8­1.

Traffic volumes expected to be generated by the related projects were calculated using rates
provided in the ITE Trip Generation manual. The related projects respective traffic generation
for the weekday AM and PM peak hours, as well as on a daily basis for a typical weekday, is
summarized in Table 8­1.

8.2        Ambient Traffic Growth
Horizon year, background traffic growth estimates have been calculated by using an ambient
traffic growth factor. The ambient traffic growth factor is intended to include unknown related
projects in the study area, as well as account for typical growth in traffic volumes due to the
development of projects outside the study area. The ambient growth factor was based on review
of the background traffic growth estimates for the Glendale area published in the 2010
Congestion Management Program, which indicate that existing traffic volumes would be
expected to increase at an annual rate of approximately 0.28 percent (0.28%) per year between
years 2010 and 2015. Thus, the annual growth rate of one percent (1.0%) increase per year to
the year 2016 is conservative for analysis purposes. Application of this ambient growth factor in
addition to the forecast traffic generated by the related projects allows for a conservative forecast
of future traffic volumes in the project study area.




LINSCOTT, LAW & GREENSPAN, engineers                                                    LLG Ref. 1-12-3981-1
                                                                                            The Link Project

                                               - 46 -
9.0        TRAFFIC IMPACT ANALYSIS
The study intersections were evaluated using the Intersection Capacity Utilization (ICU) method
of analysis which determines Volume-to-Capacity (v/c) ratios on a critical lane basis. The
overall intersection v/c ratio is subsequently assigned a Level of Service (LOS) value to describe
intersection operations. Level of Service varies from LOS A (free flow) to LOS F (jammed
condition). A description of the ICU method and corresponding Level of Service is provided in
Appendix B.

9.1        Impact Criteria and Thresholds
The relative impact of the added project traffic volumes to be generated by the proposed project
during the AM and PM peak hours was evaluated based on analysis of existing-plus-project and
future operating conditions at the study intersections, without and with the proposed project. The
previously discussed capacity analysis procedures were utilized to evaluate the future v/c
relationships and service level characteristics at each study intersection.

The significance of the potential impacts of project generated traffic at each study intersection
was identified using criteria provided by the City of Glendale Traffic & Transportation Division.
According to the City's criteria for calculating the level of impact due to traffic generated by the
proposed project, a significant transportation impact is determined based on the criteria presented
in Table 9­1.


                                                       Table 9­1
                                                  CITY OF GLENDALE
                                       INTERSECTION IMPACT THRESHOLD CRITERIA
                  Final v/c                     Level of Service      Project Related Increase in v/c
                   > 0.800                         D, E, or F           equal to or greater than 0.020


The City's criteria requires mitigation of project traffic impacts whenever traffic generated by
the proposed development causes an increase of the analyzed intersection v/c ratio by an amount
equal to or greater than the values shown above. The ICU calculations use a lane capacity of
1,600 vehicles per hour (vph) for left-turn, through, and right-turn lanes, and a dual turn lane
capacity of 2,880 vph. A clearance interval of 0.10 is also included in the ICU calculations.

11.0 OPTION 3 AND OPTION 4 PROJECT REVIEW
As described previously, the proposed project consists of the construction of a mixed-use
development with 142 apartment dwelling units and approximately 16,600 square feet of ground
floor commercial use. Four ground floor commercial development options are currently under
consideration and two consider parking on the mezzanine level. Traffic impact analyses have
been prepared for the Option 1 and 2 Projects. This chapter summarizes the qualitative review
conducted for the Option 3 and 4 Projects.

     ·     Option No. 3: Live/Work without Mezzanine Parking

                o 8,500 SF Live/Work (8 Units)

                o 8,600 SF Retail

     ·     Option No. 4: Live/Work with Mezzanine Parking

                o 8,500 SF Live/Work (8 Units)

                o 8,100 SF Retail

11.1       Option 3 Project
The Option 3 Project consists of the construction of a mixed-use development with 142
apartment dwelling units, 8 Live/Work units and 8,600 square feet of ground floor retail use.
Traffic volumes expected to be generated by the Option 3 Project were calculated using rates
provided in the ITE Trip Generation manual. As shown in Table 7-4, the Option 3 Project is
expected to generate a net increase of 40 vehicle trips (13 fewer inbound trips and 53 outbound
trips) during the AM peak hour. During the PM peak hour, the Option 3 Project is expected to
generate a net increase of 66 vehicle trips (55 inbound trips and 11 outbound trips). Over a 24-
hour period, the proposed project is forecast to generate a net increase of 834 daily trip ends
during a typical weekday (417 inbound trips and 417 outbound trips).

When compared with the trip generation forecast for the previously analyzed Option 1 Project, it
is concluded that the trip generation forecast for the Option 3 project description results in a
decrease in traffic volumes for the AM and PM peak hours, as well as on a daily basis. The trip
generation forecast for the Option 3 Project reflects decreases of 7 vehicle trips during the AM
peak hour, 12 vehicle trips during the PM peak hour, and 98 vehicle trips on a daily basis when
compared to the Option 1 Project. Thus, similar to the Option 1 Project, no significant impacts
are forecast at any of the study intersections due to the Option 3 Project and no further analysis is
required.

11.2       Option 4 Project
The Option 4 Project consists of the construction of a mixed-use development with 142
apartment dwelling units, 8 Live/Work units and 8,100 square feet of ground floor retail use with

12.0 CONGESTION MANAGEMENT PROGRAM TRAFFIC IMPACT ASSESSMENT
The Congestion Management Program (CMP) is a state-mandated program that was enacted by
the State Legislature with the passage of Proposition 111 in 1990. The program is intended to
address the impact of local growth on the regional transportation system.

As required by the 2010 Congestion Management Program, a Traffic Impact Assessment (TIA)
has been prepared to determine the potential impacts on designated monitoring locations on the
CMP highway system. The analysis has been prepared in accordance with procedures outlined
in the 2010 Congestion Management Program, Los Angeles County Metropolitan Transportation
Authority, October, 2010.

12.1       Freeways
The following CMP freeway monitoring locations in the project vicinity have been identified:

     ·     CMP Station Segment

           No. 1005              I-5 Freeway south of Colorado Boulevard Extension

           No. 1055              SR-134 Freeway east of Central Avenue

The CMP TIA guidelines require that freeway monitoring locations must be examined if the
proposed project will add 150 or more trips (in either direction) during either the AM or PM
weekday peak hours. The proposed project will not add 150 or more trips (in either direction)
during either the AM or PM weekday peak hours to the CMP freeway monitoring locations,
which is the threshold for preparing a traffic impact assessment, as stated in the CMP manual.
Therefore, no further review of potential impacts to freeway monitoring locations that are part of
the CMP highway system is required.

12.2       Intersections
There is no CMP intersection monitoring location in the project vicinity. The CMP TIA
guidelines require that intersection monitoring locations must be examined if the proposed
project will add 50 or more trips during either the AM or PM weekday peak hours (of adjacent
street traffic). The proposed project will not add 50 or more trips during the AM or PM peak
hours at any CMP monitoring intersections which is the threshold for preparing a traffic impact
assessment, as stated in the CMP manual. Therefore, no further review of potential impacts to
intersection monitoring locations that are part of the CMP highway system is required.




LINSCOTT, LAW & GREENSPAN, engineers                                                         LLG Ref. 1-12-3981-1
                                                                                                 The Link Project
                                                                                     O:\JOB_FILE\3981\Report\3981rpt.doc


                                                      - 69 -
12.3       Transit Impact Review
As required by the 2010 Congestion Management Program, a review has been made of the CMP
transit service. As previously discussed, existing transit service is provided in the vicinity of the
proposed project.

The project trip generation for the Option 1 project, as shown in Table 7­2, was adjusted by
values set forth in the CMP (i.e., person trips equal 1.4 times vehicle trips, and transit trips equal
3.5 percent of the total person trips) to estimate transit trip generation. Pursuant to the CMP
guidelines, the proposed project is forecast to generate demand for 3 transit trips during the
weekday AM peak hour, 4 transit trips during the weekday PM peak hour and 46 daily transit
trips during the weekday. The calculations are as follows:

     ·     Weekday AM Peak Hour = 47 × 1.4 × 0.035 = 3 Transit Trips

     ·     Weekday PM Peak Hour = 78 × 1.4 × 0.035 = 4 Transit Trips

     ·     Weekday Daily Trips= 932 × 1.4 × 0.035 = 46 Transit Trips

As shown in Table 5-1, 10 bus routes are provided adjacent to or in close proximity to the project
site. As outlined in Table 5-1 under the "Headways" column, these 10 transit lines provide
service for a total of 71 buses serving the project area during the weekday PM peak hour.
Therefore, based on the above calculated weekday PM peak hour transit trips, this would
correspond to an average less than one new transit rider per bus due to the proposed project. It is
anticipated that the existing transit service in the project area will adequately accommodate the
project generated transit trips. Thus, given the low number of generated transit trips per bus, no
impacts on existing or future transit services in the project area are expected to occur as a result
of the proposed project.

13.0 CALIFORNIA DEPARTMENT OF TRANSPORTATION FREEWAY IMPACT ANALYSIS
A supplemental freeway analysis was prepared based on the latest edition of the Highway
Capacity Manual (HCM 2010) operational analysis methodologies pursuant to the California
Department of Transportation's (Caltrans) Guide for the Preparation of Traffic Impact Studies 3.
According to the Caltrans document, the LOS for operating State highway facilities is based
upon measures of effectiveness (MOEs). For mainline freeway segments, the MOE is
determined based on density in passenger cars per mile per lane (pc/mi/ln). Caltrans endeavors
to maintain a target LOS at the transition between LOS "C" and LOS "D" on State highway
facilities, however, Caltrans acknowledges that this may not always be feasible and recommends
that the lead agency consult with Caltrans to determine the appropriate target LOS. If an existing
State highway facility is operating at less than the appropriate target LOS, the existing MOE
should be maintained.

The following mainline freeway segments along the I-5 Freeway have been identified for
analysis based on their proximity to the project site and are forecast to experience a relatively
greater percentage of project-related traffic than other freeway segment locations:

           I-5 Freeway north of Los Feliz Boulevard
           I-5 Freeway south of Glendale Boulevard

The impact of the project on the regional mainline freeway system has been determined based in
part on the existing weekday peak hour traffic volume data published in the 2011 Traffic
Volumes on the California State Highway System 4, and in the 2010 Congestion Management
Program. The year 2011 traffic volumes were increased by the CMP annual average growth rate
of 1.0% per year to reflect year 2013 existing conditions. This level of growth was also
compared to the percentage increase/decrease published in the 2011 Traffic Volumes on the
California State Highway System document and found to be appropriate and conservative. The
year 2013 existing traffic volumes were then increased by the CMP annual average growth rates
of 1.0% per year so as to reflect the future year 2016 analysis conditions.

The selected freeway segment lane configurations used in the analysis are based on information
obtained from field reviews. The freeway impact analysis is based on the number of mainline
freeway lanes only, including High Occupancy Vehicle lanes. Along some freeway segments,
auxiliary lanes are provided to facilitate entering and exiting freeway traffic to and from the
freeway mainline. Although some of the freeway auxiliary lanes accommodate through traffic,
these have not been considered so as to provide a conservative analysis of freeway impacts due
to the proposed project. The HCM operational analysis for freeway segments is based on density
(i.e., passenger cars per mile per lane [pc/mi/ln]).



3
  Guide for the Preparation of Traffic Impact Studies, State of California Department of Transportation, December
2002.
4
  2011 Traffic Volumes on the California State Highway System, State of California Business, Transportation and
Housing Agency, Department of Transportation Division of Traffic Operations, 2012.

existing development, and other factors, were assumed to be 1.00% per year through year 2016

and PM peak hours under the year 2016 cumulative without project conditions. With the
addition of the proposed project traffic (i.e., year 2016 cumulative with project conditions), all
study freeway segments are expected to maintain the same LOS as the year 2016 cumulative
without project conditions. As shown in Table 13-1, application of the Caltrans LOS standards
and guidelines to the year 2016 cumulative with project scenario indicates that the proposed
project is not expected to create significant impacts at any of the study freeway segments.
Incremental, but not significant, traffic impacts are noted at the study freeway segments.

14.0 CONSTRUCTION IMPACT ANALYSIS
Project construction would generate traffic from construction worker travel, as well as the arrival
and departure of trucks delivering construction materials to the site and the removal of debris
generated by on-site demolition activities. Both the number of construction workers and trucks
would vary throughout the construction process in order to maintain a reasonable schedule of
completion.

14.1       Overview of Construction Phases
The construction of the project is anticipated to consist of three phases: Demolition,
Grading/Excavation, and Sub-Grade and Above-Grade Building Construction. The total
construction period is anticipated to last approximately 24 months. The following paragraphs
provide a general overview of the various phases of construction based on information provided
by the project applicant.

14.1.1 Phase I: Demolition
This phase of construction would include the demolition and removal of the existing on-site
structures. Removal of materials would involve the use of standard construction equipment such
as loaders, dozers, backhoes, cranes and other related equipment. The duration for this phase of
construction is anticipated to be approximately one week. This work is anticipated to produce
approximately 3,544 cubic yards of export material. This corresponds to approximately 254
trucks, assuming tandem trucks with the capacity to carry up to 14 cubic yards of material per
truck. With a five day construction work week and one week duration, this phase of construction
is anticipated to generate approximately 51 truck loads per day.

14.1.2 Phase II: Grading/Excavation
This grading phase would include the excavation of existing fill materials and replacement with
properly compacted fill materials. Grading would require excavation of depths up to 22 feet
below the ground surface. Heavy construction equipment would be located on-site during
grading activities and would not travel to and from the project site on a daily basis. It is
anticipated that equipment needs associated with grading activities would include loaders,
dozers, excavators and dump trucks, and other related heavy-duty equipment. This construction
work would likely produce up to an estimated 32,800 cubic yards of soil/material export. This
corresponds to approximately 2,343 truck loads, assuming tandem trucks with the capacity to
carry 14 cubic yards of material per truck. On average, a total of 36 truck/trailer loads per day
are anticipated during this phase of construction. This phase is anticipated to be completed in
approximately three months.




LINSCOTT, LAW & GREENSPAN, engineers                                                  LLG Ref. 1-12-3981-1
                                                                                          The Link Project
                                                                              O:\JOB_FILE\3981\Report\3981rpt.doc


                                              - 74 -
14.1.3 Phase III: Sub-Grade and Above-Grade Building Construction
This phase would include the sub-grade and above grade structure construction of the project. It
is anticipated that equipment needs associated with the construction activities would include
concrete trucks, water and concrete pumps, and various miscellaneous machinery and related
equipment. During the peak period of this construction phase, a work force of approximately 90
construction workers is anticipated. Material delivery trucks and other miscellaneous trucks are
anticipated during this phase of construction. This work would likely produce an average of ten
material delivery truck trips per day. This phase is anticipated to be completed in approximately
20 months.

14.2       Construction Assumptions
It is assumed that the site would be cleared and that after completion of the first phase of short-
term construction activities (i.e., demolition, excavation and grading), trenching and building
construction would commence. The equipment staging area and construction worker parking
during the initial phases of construction grading would occur off-site. After the start of the
grading phase, the equipment staging and construction worker parking areas would be moved on-
site as space allows. While construction activity on the project site will be able to occur between
the hours of 7:00 AM and 7:00 PM, it is assumed that the majority of the workers will work
within one shift starting by 7:00 AM and concluding by 3:00 PM (with some workers ending
their workday before 3:00 PM).

14.3       Construction Traffic Trip Generation
Activities related to Phase III (Sub/Above-Grade Building Construction) would generate a higher
number of peak hour vehicle trips (combination of construction worker and truck trips) as
compared to the anticipated Phase II (Grading/Excavation) construction period. Thus, the
greatest potential for impact on the adjacent street system would occur during the building
construction phase.

14.3.1 Peak Construction Worker Demand
During the peak period of Phase III construction activities, a work force of 90 construction
workers would be required. The typical construction activity is anticipated to begin at 7:00 AM
and end at 3:00 PM. In general, the majority of the construction workers are expected to arrive
at the project site during off-peak hours (i.e., arrive prior to 7:00 AM) thereby avoiding the AM
commuter peak period. The peak hour of traffic at the study intersections along Central Avenue,
San Fernando Road, and Los Feliz Road, adjacent to the site primarily occurs between 7:00 AM
and 8:00 AM during the morning commuter period. It is anticipated that construction workers
would remain on-site throughout the day.

The number of construction worker vehicles is estimated using an average vehicle ridership
(AVR) of 1.135 persons per vehicle (as provided in the South Coast Air Quality Management
District in its CEQA Air Quality Handbook). Therefore, it is estimated that approximately 160
trips (80 inbound trips and 80 outbound trips) on a daily basis would be generated by the
construction workers during the peak construction phase at the site. The inbound construction
LINSCOTT, LAW & GREENSPAN, engineers                                                  LLG Ref. 1-12-3981-1
                                                                                          The Link Project
                                                                              O:\JOB_FILE\3981\Report\3981rpt.doc


                                                  - 75 -
worker trips would occur outside of the AM commuter peak hour; however, the outbound
construction worker trips may occur during the PM commuter peak hour. It should be noted that
the PM peak commuter period occurs between 4:00 and 6:00 PM, with little variation in traffic
flow throughout the two-hour period. Given a construction shift ending at 3:00 PM, it is
anticipated that approximately 50 percent (50%) of the construction workers would leave the site
between 3:00 and 3:30 PM, approximately 25 percent (25%) between 3:30 and 4:00 PM, and the
remaining 25 percent (25%) would leave the site between 4:00 and 4:30 PM, which overlaps
with the PM commuter peak hour. Therefore, for purposes of this analysis, it is estimated that
approximately 25 percent (25%) of the outbound construction worker trips (i.e., 20 outbound
trips) may occur during the PM commuter peak hour.

In general, it is anticipated that construction-related traffic would be largely freeway oriented.
Construction workers would likely arrive and depart via nearby on- and off-ramps serving the I-5
Freeway. The most commonly used freeway ramps would be nearest the project site, including
the I-5 Freeway ramps at Los Feliz Boulevard and Glendale Boulevard. The construction work
force would likely be generated from all parts of the Los Angeles region and are, thereby are
assumed to arrive from all directions (e.g., 20% each from SR-134 Freeway, each direction on
the I-5 Freeway, the SR-2 Freeway, and 20% from the local Glendale area). This general
distribution (i.e., 80 percent on the freeways and 20 percent on local roadways) would result in
approximately 10 vehicles at any one study intersection during the PM peak hour. This increase
is not anticipated to result in any significant impacts based on the City's significance criteria.
Further, this PM peak hour traffic increase is conservative as it does not reflect the traffic
volumes generated by the existing uses that will be removed.

Based on information provided by the project applicant, initially construction workers will park
off-site. Parking for construction workers would be provided at one or a combination of the
following locations: 1420 Central Avenue, 2861 Los Feliz Boulevard, and/or 3130 San Fernando
Road. Such off-site parking spaces shall be located within walking distance of the project site or
shuttle services will be provided by the project applicant between the off-site parking area/areas
and the project site. For final stages of construction, parking will be provided on-site.

14.3.2 Peak Construction Truck Demand
Heavy construction equipment would be located on-site during the demolition and grading
activities and would not travel to and from the project site on a daily basis. However, truck trips
would be generated so as to remove material from the site and import material to the site. Based
on information provided by the project applicant, an average of 72 truck trips per day (36
inbound trips and 36 outbound trips) is anticipated to be generated to/from the project site during
peak construction activities (i.e., Phase II: Grading/Excavation). Therefore, assuming a concrete
material delivery period of eight hours per day (beginning at 7:00 AM, with the last delivery at
3:00 PM), the 72 truck trips per day corresponds to a total of approximately 9 truck trips per
hour. Since construction truck trips would occur along major roadways with the number of truck
trips during the AM and PM peak hours being relatively limited, construction impacts from this
particular type of construction activity source are expected to be less than significant.


LINSCOTT, LAW & GREENSPAN, engineers                                                  LLG Ref. 1-12-3981-1
                                                                                          The Link Project
                                                                              O:\JOB_FILE\3981\Report\3981rpt.doc


                                              - 76 -
It is anticipated that delivery trucks/construction equipment would be brought onto the project
site and be stored within the perimeter fence of the construction site. However, temporary lane
and sidewalk closures may be required along the adjacent public streets (e.g., Central Avenue,
Los Feliz Road, San Fernando Road) to accommodate truck or equipment staging. Flagmen
would be used to control traffic movement during the ingress or egress of trucks and heavy
equipment from the construction site. As noted in Section 14.5, a Construction Traffic Control
Plan will be developed to minimize potential conflicts between construction activity and through
traffic.

14.3.3 Peak Construction Traffic Generation Summary
Taken together, the construction worker vehicles (80 inbound, 80 outbound) and concrete
material delivery trucks (5 inbound, 5 outbound) are forecast to generate 170 vehicle trips per
day (85 inbound, 85 outbound) during the peak construction phase at the site (i.e., Phase III:
Sub-Grade and Above-Grade Building Construction). It should be noted that the daily trips
generated to and from the project site during the peak construction phase are less than half of the
1,251 daily trips that will be generated by the site with the occupancy of the project.

The inbound construction worker trips are anticipated to occur outside of the AM commuter peak
hour; however, the outbound construction worker trips may overlap with the PM commuter peak
hour. It is estimated that approximately 20 outbound construction worker trips may be generated
during the PM peak hour. The construction workforce would likely be generated from all parts
of the Los Angeles region and thereby is assumed to arrive and depart from all directions (e.g.,
each direction on the I-5 Freeway, the SR-134 Freeway, the SR-2 Freeway, and from the local
Glendale area). Based on a general distribution of 80 percent on the freeways and 20 percent on
local roadways, no more than 10 vehicles are forecast at any one study intersection during the
PM peak hour. This increase is not anticipated to result in any significant impacts based on the
City's significance criteria. Therefore, the traffic impacts associated with construction activities
are determined to be less than significant.

14.4       Haul Routes
Approvals required by the City of Glendale for implementation of the proposed project include a
Truck Haul Route program approved by the City of Glendale Department of Public Works.
Based on current plans, haul trucks and delivery trucks would access the site via Los Feliz Road
and San Fernando Road. Trucks could be expected to carry the export material to the Scholl
Canyon receptor site. Haul routes shall begin from the project site to access the I-5 Freeway via
the ramps at Los Feliz Boulevard.

14.5       Construction Traffic Impacts
With the required haul route approval, the generally off-peak arrival and departure of
construction workers, and the other construction management practices described above, impacts
from construction activity are concluded to be less than significant. Impacts would be further
reduced with the implementation of the following design features:


LINSCOTT, LAW & GREENSPAN, engineers                                                   LLG Ref. 1-12-3981-1
                                                                                           The Link Project
                                                                               O:\JOB_FILE\3981\Report\3981rpt.doc


                                               - 77 -
     ·     Maintain existing access for land uses in proximity of the project site;

     ·     Limit any potential lane closures to off-peak travel periods;

     ·     Schedule receipt of construction materials during non-peak travel periods, to the extent
           possible;

     ·     Coordinate deliveries to reduce the potential of trucks waiting to unload for extended
           periods of time; and

     ·     Prohibit parking by construction workers on adjacent streets and direct construction
           workers to available parking as determined in conjunction with City staff.

In order to minimize potential conflicts between construction activity and through traffic, a
Construction Traffic Control Plan will be developed for use during project construction. The
Construction Traffic Control Plan will identify all traffic control measures, signs, and delineators
to be implemented by the construction contractor through the duration of demolition and
construction activity. In addition, the City of Glendale Department of Public Works will review
and be responsible for approval of the proposed Truck Haul Route program. Because of these
requirements and since construction-related trips would be relatively limited during the AM and
PM peak hours, construction-related transportation impacts due to the construction of the project
would be less than significant.

                                                  - 78 -
15.0 CONCLUSIONS
In order to evaluate the potential impacts due to the proposed project, five intersections were
analyzed to determine changes in operations following occupancy and utilization of the project.
It is concluded that the project (i.e., any of the four development options contained in this report)
will not create significant traffic-related impacts at any of the study intersections. Therefore, no
traffic mitigation measures are required or recommended.

In addition, freeway segments along the I-5 Freeway in the project vicinity were analyzed to
determine changes in operations following occupancy of the project. It is concluded that the
project will not create significant impacts on the I-5 Freeway segments. Therefore, no traffic
mitigation measures are required or recommended for the I-5 Freeway.

It is concluded that the proposed parking supply is expected to accommodate the forecast peak
parking demand of the project. Based on the sum of the peak parking demand requirements, the
peak parking demand for the project site is 244 spaces (176 resident spaces, 21 residential guest
spaces, and 37 commercial spaces). With the proposed parking supply of 244 spaces, the
parking supply is sufficient to meet this parking demand requirement. Thus, the parking impacts
would be considered less than significant.

A comprehensive review of potential traffic impacts during construction was also completed as
part of this traffic analysis. It was concluded that given implementation of a Construction Traffic
Control Plan; approval from the City of Glendale Department of Public Works of a Haul Route
Program; and because construction-related trips would be nominal during the AM peak hour and
less than 50 vehicles during the PM peak hour at any intersection, construction-related
transportation impacts would be less than significant.

                               INTERSECTION CAPACITY UTILIZATION (ICU) DESCRIPTION

Level of Service is a term used to describe prevailing conditions and their effect on traffic. Broadly interpreted, the Levels of Service
concept denotes any one of a number of differing combinations of operating conditions which may occur as a roadway is
accommodating various traffic volumes. Level of Service is a qualitative measure of the effect of such factors as travel speed, travel
time, traffic interruptions, freedom to maneuver, safety, driving comfort and convenience.

Six Levels of Service, A through F, have been defined in the 1965 Highway Capacity Manual, published by the Transportation Research
Board. Level of Service A describes a condition of free flow, with low traffic volumes and relatively high speeds, while Level of Service
F describes forced traffic flow at low speeds with jammed conditions and queues which cannot clear during the green phases.

The Intersection Capacity Utilization (ICU) method of intersection capacity analysis has been used in our studies. It directly relates
traffic demand and available capacity for key intersection movements, regardless of present signal timing, The capacity per hour of
green time for each approach is calculated based on the methods of the Highway Capacity Manual. The proportion of total signal time
needed by each key movement is determined and compared to the total time available (100 percent of the hour). The result of summing
the requirements of the conflicting key movements plus an allowance for clearance times is expressed as a decimal fraction. Conflicting
key traffic movements are those opposing movements whose combined green time requirements are greatest.

The resulting ICU represents the proportion of the total hour required to accommodate intersection demand volumes if the key
conflicting traffic movements are operating at capacity. Other movements may be operating near capacity, or may be operating at
significantly better levels. The ICU may be translated to a Level of Service as tabulated below.

The Levels of Service (abbreviated from the Highway Capacity Manual) are listed here with their corresponding ICU and Load Factor
equivalents. Load Factor is that proportion of the signal cycles during the peak hour which are fully loaded; i.e. when all of the vehicles
waiting at the beginning of green are not able to clear on that green phase.

                                             Intersection Capacity Utilization Characteristics
                               Level of Service                Load Factor                  Equivalent ICU
                                      A                            0.0                        0.00 - 0.60
                                      B                          0.0 - 0.1                    0.61 - 0.70
                                      C                          0.1 - 0.3                    0.71 - 0.80
                                      D                          0.3 - 0.7                    0.81 - 0.90
                                      E                          0.7 - 1.0                    0.91 - 1.00
                                      F                      Not Applicable                 Not Applicable

SERVICE LEVEL A
There are no loaded cycles and few are even close to loaded at this service level. No approach phase is fully utilized by traffic and no
vehicle waits longer than one red indication.

SERVICE LEVEL B
This level represents stable operation where an occasional approach phase is fully utilized and a substantial number are approaching full
use. Many drivers begin to feel restricted within platoons of vehicles.

SERVICE LEVEL C
At this level stable operation continues. Loading is still intermittent but more frequent than at Level B. Occasionally drivers may have
to wait through more than one red signal indication and backups may develop behind turning vehicles. Most drivers feel somewhat
restricted, but not objectionably so.

SERVICE LEVEL D
This level encompasses a zone of increasing restriction approaching instability at the intersection. Delays to approaching vehicles may
be substantial during short peaks within the peak hour, but enough cycles with lower demand occur to permit periodic clearance of
queues, thus preventing excessive backups. Drivers frequently have to wait through more than one red signal. This level is the lower
limit of acceptable operation to most drivers.

SERVICE LEVEL E
This represents near capacity and capacity operation. At capacity (ICU = 1.0) it represents the most vehicles that the particular
intersection can accommodate. However, full utilization of every signal cycle is seldom attained no matter how great the demand. At
this level all drivers wait through more than one red signal, and frequently through several.

SERVICE LEVEL F
Jammed conditions. Traffic backed up from a downstream location on one of the street restricts or prevents movement of traffic through
the intersection under consideration.
